CRI-O randomly opens ephemeral TCP ports (range 32768–60999) on nodes that have no EndpointSlice. Previously, the Linux ephemeral port range (32768–60999) was included in `commatrix.DynamicRanges`, and `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges()` in `validation_test.go:159` would silently exclude them. PR #400 (`7d56343`, "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix") stripped the ephemeral range from `DynamicRanges` to fix firewall over-permissiveness. Without that range, the 5 crio ephemeral ports survive both filters (`filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` only strips `rpc.statd`/`dnsmasq`/`dig`) and reach the `Fail()` at line 161. -
Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** CRI-O ephemeral TCP ports lack EndpointSlices and are no longer filtered after Linux dynamic range removal. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: crio ephemeral ports no longer filtered by dynamic range** (affects Tests: `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAIL] Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports /tmp/secret/commatrix/test/e2e/validation_test.go:161 ``` From `matrix-diff-ss`: ``` - Ingress,TCP,40143,,crio,,,master,false - Ingress,TCP,43283,,crio,,,master,false - Ingress,TCP,45787,,crio,,,master,false - Ingress,TCP,33839,,crio,,,worker,false - Ingress,TCP,38471,,crio,,,worker,false ``` - **Root Cause:** CRI-O randomly opens ephemeral TCP ports (range 32768–60999) on nodes that have no EndpointSlice. Previously, the Linux ephemeral port range (32768–60999) was included in `commatrix.DynamicRanges`, and `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges()` in `validation_test.go:159` would silently exclude them. PR #400 (`7d56343`, "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix") stripped the ephemeral range from `DynamicRanges` to fix firewall over-permissiveness. Without that range, the 5 crio ephemeral ports survive both filters (`filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` only strips `rpc.statd`/`dnsmasq`/`dig`) and reach the `Fail()` at line 161. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** PR #400 — commit `7d56343` / merge `1fec55d` ("Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix"). Backport status to `release-5.0` could not be verified (remote branch not fetched locally); the failure pattern is consistent with this change being present on `release-5.0` since the test code was cloned from that branch. - **Is it a flake?** No — crio consistently opens ephemeral listener sockets; without the dynamic range filter this will recur every run. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `crio` to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` exclusion list in `validation_test.go` (alongside `rpc.statd`), or reintroduce a CRI-O-specific ephemeral range entry in the test's `DynamicRanges` without reopening the full Linux ephemeral range. Alternatively, tag crio ephemeral ports as `Optional: true` and skip them in the EPS validation. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause group. The secondary mismatch (6 ports in matrix but not in use: TCP 8798 `machine-config-daemon`, TCP 9192 `machine-approver`, TCP 9443 `cloud-controller-manager-operator`, UDP 68 `NetworkManager` on master/worker) produced only a `logrus.Warningf` and did not cause a test failure. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 5.0 (release-5.0) — 1 of 4 specs failed; nftables reboot test and doc-diff test passed. **Affected Images:** `ci/telco-runner:latest`, `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release-5:5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-07-10-030545` (cluster image, not the commatrix test binary itself) **Overall Issue Class:** `matrix_mismatch` **Overall Severity:** HIGH

The crio container runtime binds to random ephemeral TCP ports (36791, 38429, 39393, 40411, 40547, 42339 — all in Linux ephemeral range 32768–60999). In `validation_test.go:157–161`, `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` only skips `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, and `dig` — not `crio`. Then `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` (line 159) uses `commatrix.DynamicRanges` which (since commit 7d56343) only covers KubeletNodePort 30000–32767, not the Linux ephemeral range. The crio ports (all > 32767) survive both filters and trigger `Fail()` at line 161. Commit 7d56343 (`Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix`, PR #400, Feb 5 2026) is the first domino: it intentionally removed the Linux ephemeral range from `KubeletNodePortDefaultDynamicRange` and from the generated commatrix's dynamic ranges, but left the test's `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` with no coverage above 32767. -

In `validation_test.go:157–161`, `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` only skips `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, and `dig` — not `crio`. Then `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` (line 159) uses `commatrix.DynamicRanges` which (since commit 7d56343) only covers KubeletNodePort 30000–32767, not the Linux ephemeral range. The crio ports (all > 32767) survive both filters and trigger `Fail()` at line 161. Commit 7d56343 (`Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix`, PR #400, Feb 5 2026) is the first domino: it intentionally removed the Linux ephemeral range from `KubeletNodePortDefaultDynamicRange` and from the generated commatrix's dynamic ranges, but left the test's `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` with no coverage above 32767. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/commit/7d56343 (PR #400, merged on `main`; also present on `release-4.23` as evidenced by the CI checkout running the identical test code and communication-matrix.csv containing only the 30000-32767 range) - **Is it a flake?** No — crio always holds ephemeral sockets during operation; this will fail on every run until `crio` is added to `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` or its ephemeral range is added back as a non-firewall dynamic range. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `crio` to the known-services skip list in `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (`validation_test.go:221–239`), analogous to how `rpc.statd` is handled; or add a separate "host-process ephemeral" dynamic range (32768–60999) in the test that is used only for filtering — not for nftables firewall generation. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause. The removal of Linux ephemeral dynamic ranges (7d56343) left crio's random ports unfiltered in the one test that checks for undocumented open ports with no EndpointSlice. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 4.23 — 1 of 4 specs failed; 3 passed (nftables reboot check passed, doc-matrix comparison passed, static entries check passed). **Affected Images:** `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.23.0-0.nightly-2026-07-03-022524`; commatrix test image (built from `release-4.23` branch of `github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix`) **Overall Issue Class:** matrix_mismatch **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM

The test at `validation_test.go:159` calls `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)` — but `commatrix.DynamicRanges` is now empty, so the filter is a no-op. Crio binds to random ephemeral ports (32768–60999) on each node IP, which previously fell inside the dynamic range and were silently filtered. `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` at line 157 also does not handle `crio` (only `rpc.statd` and `dnsmasq`). Both filters now fail to exclude these ports, exposing the regression. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** `7d56343` / PR #400 — `https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/pull/400` - **Is it a flake?** No — crio always binds ephemeral ports on startup; the specific port numbers vary per run but the failure reproduces on every job. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `"crio"` to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` allowlist in `test/e2e/validation_test.go:221–239`, or restore ephemeral-range filtering specifically for the EndpointSlice check (separate from the matrix generation path). Alternatively, investigate whether crio's gRPC stream-server ports should carry a static `ComDetails` entry so they match an EndpointSlice. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (`validation_test.go:141`) --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause group. The 7 stale matrix entries (`6388`, `8798` ×2, `9192`, `9443`, `UDP/68` ×2) only produce log warnings (`logrus.Warningf` at line 154) and do not contribute to the test failure; they represent documentation drift independent of the crio regression. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 5.0 (nightly 2026-06-22-235733) — failure is deterministic on this version due to missing dynamic-range filtering for crio ephemeral ports. **Affected Images:** `ci/telco-runner:latest` (test runner), `ocp-kni/test:dev-scripts` (cluster setup); no image pull errors — all images pulled successfully. **Overall Issue Class:** `test_regression` **Overall Severity:** HIGH

CRI-O (the container runtime, PID 2709) opens a randomly-assigned ephemeral port (36239, in the Linux range 32768–60999) that has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice. `validation_test.go:159` calls `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)`, but `commatrix.DynamicRanges` is populated by `GetDynamicRanges()` (`pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go`) which returns only the Kubernetes NodePort range (30000–32767). Port 36239 > 32767, so it is not filtered. Prior to PR #400 (`7d56343`), the Linux ephemeral range was included in `DynamicRanges` and this port would have been filtered; that PR removed it to prevent the firewall matrix from leaving all ephemeral ports open, but also broke the EPS validation filter. -
Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** CRI-O's ephemeral port (36239) is open but has no EndpointSlice and is not filtered after PR #400 removed Linux dynamic ranges. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: CRI-O ephemeral port not filtered by EPS validation test** (affects Tests: `[It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAIL] Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports /tmp/secret/commatrix/test/e2e/validation_test.go:161 ``` `Port 36239: LISTEN 0 4096 10.0.1.66:36239 0.0.0.0:* users:(("crio",pid=2709,fd=12))` `matrix-diff-ss: - Ingress,TCP,36239,,crio,,,master,false` - **Root Cause:** CRI-O (the container runtime, PID 2709) opens a randomly-assigned ephemeral port (36239, in the Linux range 32768–60999) that has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice. `validation_test.go:159` calls `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)`, but `commatrix.DynamicRanges` is populated by `GetDynamicRanges()` (`pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go`) which returns only the Kubernetes NodePort range (30000–32767). Port 36239 > 32767, so it is not filtered. Prior to PR #400 (`7d56343`), the Linux ephemeral range was included in `DynamicRanges` and this port would have been filtered; that PR removed it to prevent the firewall matrix from leaving all ephemeral ports open, but also broke the EPS validation filter. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** `1fec55d` Merge pull request #400 from shirmoran/remove-linux-dynamic-range (`7d56343` "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix") - **Is it a flake?** No — CRI-O consistently opens an ephemeral port above 32767 on every cluster, so this failure will recur on every run until fixed. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `"crio"` to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` allowlist in `test/e2e/validation_test.go` (alongside the existing `rpc.statd` filter), since CRI-O is a host-level process that opens random ephemeral ports with no EndpointSlice by design. Alternatively, add a separate Linux ephemeral range filter (32768–60999) to the EPS validation check without putting it back into the generated firewall matrix. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause. The 7 stale matrix entries (TCP 80, 443, 8798, 9099, 9192, 9443, 10258 — documented or EPS-generated but not actually open on the SNO node) generate only `logrus.Warning` calls (lines 108–110 and 153–155 of `validation_test.go`) and do not fail any test. They indicate the `docs/stable/raw/aws-sno.csv` documented matrix is drifting from actual OCP 4.23 SNO port usage but are not the direct failure cause. **Per-Version Notes:** - OCP 4.23 (evidence): CRI-O ephemeral port 36239 fails the EPS validation; 7 stale matrix entries logged as warnings. - OCP 5.0 (no evidence file): Same root cause expected — identical `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` logic and `GetDynamicRanges` returning only NodePort range; CRI-O ephemeral port behavior unchanged. **Affected Images:** `ci/telco-runner:latest` (test runner); OCP release `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.23.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-155843` **Overall Issue Class:** `matrix_mismatch` **Overall Severity:** HIGH

The `telco5g-sno-setup` step ran an Ansible playbook (`ocp-install.yml`) to provision an OCP 4.21 nightly SNO cluster on bare metal node `cnfdu14.upstreamci.bos2.lab`. After ~2.5 hours, the cluster API server at `192.168.17.121:6443` was still completely unreachable ("no route to host"), meaning the install never completed or the node never came up. The "RETRYING: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready" failures are Ansible retry loop iterations in `ocp-install.yml` (lines 38/46/58) waiting for the API — not commatrix test assertions. The commatrix project tests were never reached. -
Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** Bare metal SNO cluster install failed — API server never reachable, commatrix tests never ran. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: Bare-metal SNO cluster provisioning failure** (affects all reported "tests") - **Evidence:** ``` E0625 11:38:33.348497 1755289 memcache.go:265] couldn't get current server API group list: Get "https://api.cnfdu14.upstreamci.bos2.lab:6443/api?timeout=32s": dial tcp 192.168.17.121:6443: connect: no route to host "telco5g-network-flow-matrix-single-node-bm-telco5g-sno-setup" failed after 2h34m42s (failed containers: test): ContainerFailed — Container test exited with code 2 PLAY RECAP: XXXXXXXXXXXX ok=0 changed=0 unreachable=0 failed=1 skipped=0 ``` - **Root Cause:** The `telco5g-sno-setup` step ran an Ansible playbook (`ocp-install.yml`) to provision an OCP 4.21 nightly SNO cluster on bare metal node `cnfdu14.upstreamci.bos2.lab`. After ~2.5 hours, the cluster API server at `192.168.17.121:6443` was still completely unreachable ("no route to host"), meaning the install never completed or the node never came up. The "RETRYING: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready" failures are Ansible retry loop iterations in `ocp-install.yml` (lines 38/46/58) waiting for the API — not commatrix test assertions. The commatrix project tests were never reached. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — this is an infrastructure/bare-metal provisioning failure, not a code regression. - **Is it a flake?** Yes — "no route to host" on a bare metal lab node is consistent with a transient hardware, network, or OCP installer issue on this specific machine. - **Suggested Fix:** Retry the job. If it fails again on the same node (`cnfdu14`), investigate the bare metal host health (BMC/IPMI, NIC, routing) and whether the OCP 4.21 nightly `2026-06-25-024321` installer is healthy. - **Affected tests:** - `RETRYING: [XXXXXXXXXXXX]: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready (60 retries left)` - `RETRYING: [XXXXXXXXXXXX]: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready (59 retries left)` - `RETRYING: [XXXXXXXXXXXX]: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready (58 retries left)` - `RETRYING: [XXXXXXXXXXXX]: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready (57 retries left)` - `RETRYING: [XXXXXXXXXXXX]: Run oc command to check if cluster is ready (56 retries left)` --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause — all failures cascade from the SNO cluster never becoming ready. Gather steps (must-gather, extra, audit-logs, telco5g-log-gather) all failed for the same reason: TLS handshake timeouts / no route to host against the same dead API endpoint. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 4.21 nightly `2026-06-25-024321` — cluster import succeeded in ci-operator (190 images), but bare metal install of this nightly on `cnfdu14` failed. **Affected Images:** `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release:4.21.0-0.nightly-2026-06-25-024321` (used for SNO install); `ci/telco-runner:latest` (CI orchestration image — pulled successfully). **Overall Issue Class:** `infra_other` **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM

The API server got `connection refused` when dialing the node's kubelet port 10250, meaning kubelet's exec endpoint was unreachable on that node. The most likely cause on a reused bare-metal cluster is residual nftables rules from a prior periodic CI run that did not include port 10250 in the allow list; the generated `communication-matrix-worker.nft` for this run does include port 10250, but that rule had not yet been applied when the test started. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — no recent code change caused this; it's a cluster-state issue. Alternatively, add a retry or wait loop in `GenerateSS` to tolerate transient kubelet exec failures. - **Affected tests:** - `Validation [BeforeEach] generated communication matrix should be equal to documented communication matrix` (`validation_test.go:62`) - `Validation [BeforeEach] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (`validation_test.go:138`) --- **Relation Between Groups:** Single root cause — both Validation tests share the same BeforeEach block (`validation_test.go:41–64`) and both failed on the identical error. The crio container runtime is listening on ephemeral TCP port 34279 bound to the specific node IP `10.0.91.164` (not `0.0.0.0`). This port has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice (it is a host-level process, not a Kubernetes Service), and it is not present in the documented communication matrix. The test at `validation_test.go:161` strictly requires every detected open port to have a backing EndpointSlice, so crio's untracked socket causes a hard FAIL. The port number (within Linux ephemeral range 32768–60999) is randomly assigned by the OS and will differ on each reboot or crio restart. -
Full analysis
--- **TL;DR:** OCP 5.0 SNO port landscape diverged from commatrix: 1 crio ephemeral port causes hard fail, 4 stale matrix entries, 2 cloud-controller ports missing EndpointSlice. **Root Cause Groups:** - **Group 1: crio ephemeral port open with no EndpointSlice** (affects Tests: `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports`) - **Evidence:** ``` [FAILED] the following ports are used but don't have an endpointslice: Ingress,TCP,34279,,crio,,,master,false ``` ``` Port 34279: LISTEN 0 4096 10.0.91.164:34279 0.0.0.0:* users:(("crio",pid=4133,fd=12)) ``` - **Root Cause:** The crio container runtime is listening on ephemeral TCP port 34279 bound to the specific node IP `10.0.91.164` (not `0.0.0.0`). This port has no Kubernetes EndpointSlice (it is a host-level process, not a Kubernetes Service), and it is not present in the documented communication matrix. The test at `validation_test.go:161` strictly requires every detected open port to have a backing EndpointSlice, so crio's untracked socket causes a hard FAIL. The port number (within Linux ephemeral range 32768–60999) is randomly assigned by the OS and will differ on each reboot or crio restart. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — this appears to be a new crio behavior in OCP 5.0 nightly `5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-153432`; no specific PR identified. - **Is it a flake?** Potentially yes — the ephemeral port number changes every reboot, meaning the port may not always be visible at test-capture time, but the underlying condition (crio listening on a node-IP-bound port with no EndpointSlice) is structural. - **Suggested Fix:** Either add a static commatrix entry for crio's metrics/stream socket on the node IP (with `Optional:true`), or update the test's EndpointSlice validation to exclude ports belonging to known host-level processes (crio, rpcbind, rpc.statd) that cannot have EndpointSlices by design. - **Affected tests:** `Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` (`validation_test.go:161`) - **Group 2: Stale documented-matrix entries — services not running on OCP 5.0 SNO AWS** (affects: warning emitted, contributes to "6 in matrix but not in use" count) - **Evidence:** ``` level=warning msg="the following ports are documented but are not used: Ingress,TCP,80,openshift-ingress,router-default,... Ingress,TCP,443,openshift-ingress,router-default,... Ingress,TCP,8798,openshift-machine-config-operator,machine-config-daemon,... Ingress,TCP,9192,openshift-cluster-machine-approver,machine-approver,..." ``` ``` # matrix-diff-summary.txt: Ports in matrix but not in use on node: Ingress,TCP,80 / 443 / 8798 / 9192 / 9443 / 10258 ``` - **Root Cause:** Four ports (TCP 80, 443, 8798, 9192) exist in the documented OCP 5.0 commatrix but are not open on the single-node AWS cluster. Router ports 80/443 may not be active on SNO, `machine-config-daemon` port 8798 (internal health) moved or was removed, and the `machine-approver` kube-rbac-proxy port 9192 is absent. These are stale entries in `doc/aws-sno` commatrix CSV that were never updated for OCP 5.0 / SNO topology changes. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — likely reflects incremental OCP 5.0 component changes that were never reconciled back into the commatrix docs. - **Is it a flake?** No — these ports are consistently absent on SNO; this is a documentation gap. - **Suggested Fix:** Remove TCP 80, 443, 8798, 9192 from the documented AWS SNO commatrix, or mark them `Optional:true` with an SNO-exception note. - **Affected tests:** Logged as warnings; does not directly fail a test but inflates the "6 in matrix but not in use" count reported in the job reason. - **Group 3: Cloud-controller-manager ports open but missing EndpointSlice** (affects: "open but missing endpointslice" count) - **Evidence:** ``` # matrix-diff-summary.txt: Ports open but missing EndpointSlice: Ingress,TCP,9443,openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator,...cluster-cloud-controller-manager... Ingress,TCP,10258,openshift-cloud-controller-manager,aws-cloud-controller-manager,... ``` ``` level=warning msg="the following ports are not used: Ingress,TCP,9443,... Ingress,TCP,10258,...\n" ``` - **Root Cause:** TCP 9443 (`cloud-controller-manager-operator`) and TCP 10258 (`aws-cloud-controller-manager`) are actively listening on the node but have no corresponding EndpointSlice. These are OCP platform services (not commatrix code). The documented matrix still lists them as EndpointSlice-backed entries. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** Unknown — likely an upstream OCP 5.0 cloud-controller-manager architecture change; see `openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator` release notes for OCP 5.0. - **Is it a flake?** No — this is a structural gap: the cloud-controller services consistently lack EndpointSlice in OCP 5.0 SNO. - **Suggested Fix:** File a Jira against `openshift-cloud-controller-manager-operator` to ensure an EndpointSlice is created for ports 9443/10258, or update the commatrix static-entries to mark these as host-process ports not requiring EndpointSlice validation. - **Affected tests:** Does not fail the test directly (treated as warning), but contributes to the "open but missing endpointslice" count in the job failure reason. --- **Relation Between Groups:** All three groups share the same upstream cause: the OCP 5.0 SNO platform port landscape has drifted from the commatrix documentation and assumptions. Group 1 is the only hard test failure; Groups 2 and 3 are unresolved data inconsistencies that inflate the mismatch counts. There is no image pull failure or CI infrastructure failure — the cluster deployed successfully and 3 of 4 test specs passed. **Per-Version Notes:** OCP 5.0 (`5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-153432`, SNO/AWS/OVN) — commatrix docs need updating for SNO topology; cloud-controller-manager EndpointSlice gap is specific to 5.0 architecture. **Affected Images:** `quay.io/openshift-release-dev/ocp-v5.0-art-dev@sha256:c439d20d39a77f862424a2f194f44b9789091e7523ae82c514ee0b0205b2d8ae` (test runner); OCP release `registry.ci.openshift.org/ocp/release-5:5.0.0-0.nightly-2026-06-24-153432` **Overall Issue Class:** matrix_mismatch **Overall Severity:** MEDIUM — the cluster and workloads are healthy; the failure reflects documentation/EndpointSlice gaps, not a broken OCP component. The port numbers change per run (ephemeral), but crio ports in 32768–60999 with no EndpointSlice will always appear. Every run since PR #400 merged will trigger this failure. - **Suggested Fix:** Extend `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices()` in `validation_test.go` to also skip entries where `Service == "crio"` (matching the same pattern already used for `rpc.statd`). This is the minimal, targeted fix that doesn't reintroduce the broad ephemeral range into the generated matrix. Port TCP 44463 is bound by the CRI-O container runtime process (pid=2677) as an ephemeral host-level socket (`LISTEN 0 4096 10.0.82.179:44463 0.0.0.0:*`). Because it is a host process, no Kubernetes EndpointSlice exists for it. Prior to PR #400, the generated `commatrix.DynamicRanges` included the Linux ephemeral private port range (32768–60999), and the call to `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` at `validation_test.go:159` would have silently discarded port 44463 (which falls in that range). PR #400 removed `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange` from `pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go` and deleted `types.LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange`, leaving only the Kubernetes NodePort range (30000–32767) as a dynamic filter. Port 44463 is outside that range, and `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (`validation_test.go:221–239`) only exempts `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, and `dig` — not `crio` — so the port survives all filtering and causes the `Fail` at line 161. -

Because it is a host process, no Kubernetes EndpointSlice exists for it. Prior to PR #400, the generated `commatrix.DynamicRanges` included the Linux ephemeral private port range (32768–60999), and the call to `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` at `validation_test.go:159` would have silently discarded port 44463 (which falls in that range). PR #400 removed `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange` from `pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go` and deleted `types.LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange`, leaving only the Kubernetes NodePort range (30000–32767) as a dynamic filter. Port 44463 is outside that range, and `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (`validation_test.go:221–239`) only exempts `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, and `dig` — not `crio` — so the port survives all filtering and causes the `Fail` at line 161. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** [PR #400 — "Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix"](https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/pull/400) — merged 2026-04-28, commit `7d56343e0d6e32f2fcc9b639ada47bb83cc57740`. The specific change that broke the test was the deletion of `LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange` from `pkg/types/static-custom-entries.go` and the removal of `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange` from `pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go`, which together stripped the 32768–60999 dynamic-range filter from the validation path. - **Source File:** https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/blob/main/test/e2e/validation_test.go#L161 - **Is it a flake?** Likely yes for the specific port number, but structurally a deterministic regression. Port 44463 is an ephemeral OS-assigned port; on any given run the exact port number from CRI-O will differ, but CRI-O consistently opens an ephemeral host-level socket (for internal streaming/gRPC) that lands in the 32768–60999 range. Before PR #400, every such port was silently filtered. After PR #400, every run where CRI-O's ephemeral port lands outside 30000–32767 (i.e. practically every run) will fail. The failure mode is therefore structurally consistent, even if the exact port number varies per run. - **Suggested Fix:** Add `crio` (and potentially any other known container-runtime host processes) to the `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` function in `test/e2e/validation_test.go`, following the same pattern already used for `rpc.statd` (line 226–229). CRI-O is a host-level daemon that will never have an EndpointSlice; treating it exactly like `rpc.statd` is the correct semantic. A broader but also valid fix is to re-introduce the Linux ephemeral range as a separate, test-only filter (not in the firewall matrix), so any ephemeral host process is automatically excluded from the EPS validation without re-opening the firewall concern that motivated PR #400. --- **Relation Between Failures:** There is only one failed test. The OpenShift e2e suite runner includes background MonitorTests that continuously observe cluster health (metrics API availability, operator state, node readiness, timeline). The commatrix test suite deliberately reboots the single node to verify nftables rules survive a reboot (`nftables-after-reboot-ip-10-0-5-59.ec2.internal` artifact confirms reboot happened). During that reboot the node transitions to `NotReady`, which is a normal and expected part of the test. However, the MonitorTest framework — which is not aware that the reboot is intentional — flags the `node-not-ready` interval as a test failure. The commatrix project's own tests finished successfully ~44 minutes in (sidecar upload at 14:01:38 UTC), but the MonitorTest harness continued running until it declared failure at 15:51:13 UTC. -

--- ### Test 1: `[TestE2e] Validation [It] should validate the communication matrix ports match the node's open ports` - **Duration:** 46.796 seconds - **Error:** `the following ports are used but don't have an endpointslice: Ingress,TCP,39293,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,41719,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,42319,,crio,,,master,false Ingress,TCP,33183,,crio,,,worker,false Ingress,TCP,33893,,crio,,,worker,false Ingress,TCP,46631,,crio,,,worker,false` - **Root Cause:** The test at `validation_test.go:161` calls `Fail()` when any open-node ports survive two successive filter passes — `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (line 157) and `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` (line 159). Six TCP ports opened by the `crio` container-runtime on master-1 (39293), master-0 (41719, 42319), worker-0 (33183), worker-2 (33893), and worker-1 (46631) are all in the Linux ephemeral range (32768–60999). They appear in the raw `ss` output and thus in `matrix-diff-ss` as `-` (Missing) entries, but they are not backed by Kubernetes EndpointSlices. `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` only skips `rpc.statd` and `dnsmasq`/`dig` — it has no rule for `crio`. `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` uses `commatrix.DynamicRanges`, which after PR #400 contains only TCP/UDP 30000–32767 (Kubelet NodePort range); all six crio ports fall in 32768–60999 and are **not** covered by that range. Before PR #400, `commatrix.DynamicRanges` also included `LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange` (32768–60999), which would have filtered these ports out; its removal is the direct cause of the regression. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/pull/400 — commit `7d56343e0d6e32f2fcc9b639ada47bb83cc57740` ("Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix"), merged April 28 2026 as `1fec55d`. The commit intentionally removed the Linux ephemeral dynamic range from the firewall-facing commatrix (valid rationale: keeping that range in nftables rules would open all 28 000+ ports). The side-effect is that the **test-side** `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges` call that previously relied on that range to suppress crio ephemeral ports now no longer filters them. - **Source File:** https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/blob/main/test/e2e/validation_test.go#L141 - **Is it a flake?** No. The `crio` container-runtime opens per-node gRPC/health-check sockets in the OS ephemeral range on every cluster boot; they consistently appear in `ss` output and consistently lack EndpointSlice records. The `raw-ss-tcp` evidence shows them bound on dedicated node IPs (e.g., `192.168.111.21:39293 crio pid=3007`) — not transient connections. This failure will recur on every run until the filter is corrected. - **Suggested Fix:** In `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (`validation_test.go:221`), add a case to skip entries whose `Service` field is `"crio"` (mirroring the existing `rpc.statd` exclusion), since crio opens these sockets for container-runtime-internal communications that will never have a Kubernetes EndpointSlice. A complementary option is to introduce a test-only `LinuxEphemeralRange` dynamic-range variable (32768–60999 TCP+UDP) appended to `commatrix.DynamicRanges` only inside the validation test, keeping it absent from any firewall-rule generation path. --- **Relation Between Failures:** There is only one failing test in this run. The prompt's summary figure of "10 port(s) in matrix but not in use" describes stale entries in the _documented_ bm.csv (metal3/MCD/machine-approver ports no longer present on the cluster), surfaced as warnings by the passing `generated communication matrix should be equal to documented communication matrix` test — those are not the cause of the CI failure. All failures trace to a single root cause: the removal of the Linux ephemeral dynamic range in PR #400 breaking the crio-port filter in the second validation test. **Affected Images:** - `registry.ci.openshift.org/openshift-kni/commatrix:latest` (the `oc commatrix` plug

They appear in `ss` output but have no backing EndpointSlice, so they land in `missingEPSMat` (lines prefixed with `-` in `matrix-diff-ss`). The test applies two filters: `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (line 157) — which only skips `rpc.statd`, `dnsmasq`, and `dig`, not `crio` — and then `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, commatrix.DynamicRanges)` (line 159). Previously, `commatrix.DynamicRanges` included the Linux ephemeral range (32768–60999 via `types.LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange`), which silently absorbed these crio ports. PR #400 (commit `7d56343`) deliberately removed `getLinuxDynamicPrivateRange` from `GetDynamicRanges` in `pkg/dynamic-ranges/dynamic-ranges.go` and also dropped the corresponding `append(...LinuxDynamicPrivateDefaultDynamicRange...)` from `test/e2e/validation_test.go` (only the doc-matrix test path was patched). After the removal, `commatrix.DynamicRanges` only contains the Kubelet NodePort range (30000–32767); all six crio ephemeral ports (≥ 32768) are no longer filtered and fall through to the `Fail()` call. - **Breaking PR/Commit:** - Commit: [`7d56343`](https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/commit/7d56343e0d6e32f2fcc9b639ada47bb83cc57740) — *"Remove Linux Dynamic ranges from generated communication matrix"* - Merged via PR #400 as merge commit [`1fec55d`](https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/commit/1fec55d18941decd14478d746fc641063a435d69) on 2026-04-28 - **Source File:** https://github.com/openshift-kni/commatrix/blob/main/test/e2e/validation_test.go#L141-L163 — the failing `It` block; the assertion fires at line 161 - **Is it a flake?** No. CRI-O consistently opens ephemeral gRPC streaming ports (confirmed via `ss` on master-0, master-2, worker-0, worker-1, worker-2). The port numbers change per-run but they always land in the 32768–60999 ephemeral range. The failure is fully deterministic: every time `commatrix.DynamicRanges` lacks the Linux ephemeral range, these ports will reach `Fail()`. - **Suggested Fix:** In `test/e2e/validation_test.go`, add `crio` to `filterOutPortsOfKnownServices` (lines 221–239), since crio ephemeral ports are a known host-level gRPC mechanism with no EndpointSlice by design. Alternatively — and more robustly — re-introduce a separate ephemeral-range exemption list used *only* in the validation filter (decoupled from nftables generation, which was the correct motivation of PR #400): call `filterOutPortsInDynamicRanges(missingEPSMat, types.LinuxEphemeralDynamicRange)` before the `Fail` check, where `LinuxEphemeralDynamicRange` defines 32768–60999 for both TCP and UDP. This preserves PR #400's intent (no ephemeral range in generated firewall rules) while still exempting ephemeral host-process ports from the EndpointSlice check. --- **Relation Between Failures:** There is only one failing Ginkgo `It` block. The error output in the prompt lists sub-steps (test phase messages and the specific port list) that all belong to the same single test.
